[30;1m549 | [0m[35m* You need fault tolerance (scheduling will continue even if a node or process running[0m
[30;1m550 | [0m[35m  a scheduler goes down)[0m
[30;1m551 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m552 | [0m[35mWhen you have multiple schedulers running at once, they need to be able to coordinate[0m
[30;1m553 | [0m[35mtheir efforts so that the schedules don't get processed more than once and the[0m

[30;1m223 | [0m[35mScheduling tasks[0m
[30;1m224 | [0m[35m================[0m
[30;1m225 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m226 | [0m[35mTo create a schedule for running a task, you need, at the minimum:[0m
[30;1m227 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m228 | [0m[35m* A preconfigured task_, OR a callable_ to be run[0m
[30;1m229 | [0m[35m* A trigger_[0m

[31m--[ [0m[34mMatch #[0m[33m64[0m[34m of [0m[33m384[0m[31m ]--[0m

[30;1m28 | [0m[35m============[0m
[30;1m29 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m30 | [0m[35mThe core concept of APScheduler is to give the user the ability to queue Python code to[0m
[30;1m31 | [0m[35mbe executed, either as soon as possible, later at a given time, or on a recurring[0m
[30;1m32 | [0m[35mschedule.[0m
[30;1m33 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m34 | [0m[35mThe *scheduler* is the user-facing interface of the system. When it's running, it does[0m

[31m--[ [0m[34mMatch #[0m[33m65[0m[34m of [0m[33m384[0m[31m ]--[0m
   Rule Id: [34mBD000610[0m
       Tag: [34mSecurity.Backdoor.LOLBAS.Linux[0m
  Severity: [36mModerate[0m, Confidence: [36mLow[0m

   Pattern: [32m\s(apt|apt\-get|aria2c|arp|ash|awk|base64|bash|bpftrace|busybox|cat|chmod|chown|cp|cpan|cpulimit|crontab|csh|curl|cut|dash|dd|diff|dmesg|dmsetup|dnf|docker|dpkg|easy_install|ed|emacs|env|expand|expect|facter|find|finger|flock|fmt|ftp|gawk|gdb|gimp|git|grep|head|iftop|ionice|ip|irb|jjs|journalctl|jrunscript|ksh|ld\.so|ldconfig|logsave|ltrace|lua|mail|mawk|mount|mtr|mv|mysql|nano|nawk|nc|nice|nl|nmap|node|od|openssl|perl|pg|php|pic|pico|pip|puppet|readelf|red|rlogin|rlwrap|rpm|rpmquery|rsync|ruby|run\-mailcap|run\-parts|rvim|scp|screen|script|sed|service|setarch|sftp|shuf|smbclient|socat|sort|sqlite3|ssh|start\-stop\-daemon|stdbuf|strace|systemctl|tail|tar|taskset|tclsh|tcpdump|tee|telnet|tftp|time|timeout|tmux|top|ul|unexpand|uniq|unshare|vi|vim|watch|wget|whois|wish|xargs|xxd|yum|zsh|zypper)\s[0m
[30;1m554 | [0m[35mschedulers know when to wake up even if another scheduler added the next due schedule to[0m
[30;1m555 | [0m[35mthe data store. To this end, a shared *event broker* must be configured.[0m
[30;1m556 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m557 | [0m[35m.. seealso:: You can find practical examples of data store sharing in the[0m
[30;1m558 | [0m[35m    :file:`examples/web` directory.[0m
[30;1m559 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m560 | [0m[35mUsing a scheduler without running it[0m

[31m--[ [0m[34mMatch #[0m[33m66[0m[34m of [0m[33m384[0m[31m ]--[0m

[30;1m546 | [0m[35mthe same data store at once:[0m
[30;1m547 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m548 | [0m[35m* Running a server application (usually a web app) with multiple worker processes[0m
[30;1m549 | [0m[35m* You need fault tolerance (scheduling will continue even if a node or process running[0m
[30;1m550 | [0m[35m  a scheduler goes down)[0m

[30;1m49 | [0m[35minternal state needs to be updated before returning to ensure that the trigger won't[0m
[30;1m50 | [0m[35mreturn the same datetime on the next call. The trigger code does **not** need to be[0m
[30;1m51 | [0m[35mthread-safe.[0m
